**OpenAI Codex**

<permissions instructions>
Filesystem sandboxing defines which files can be read or written. `sandbox_mode` is `workspace-write`: The sandbox permits reading files, and editing files in `cwd` and `writable_roots`. Editing files in other directories requires approval. Network access is restricted.
# Escalation Requests

Commands are run outside the sandbox if they are approved by the user, or match an existing rule that allows it to run unrestricted. The command string is split into independent command segments at shell control operators, including but not limited to:

- Pipes: |
- Logical operators: &&, ||
- Command separators: ;
- Subshell boundaries: (...), $(...)

Each resulting segment is evaluated independently for sandbox restrictions and approval requirements.

Example:

git pull | tee output.txt

This is treated as two command segments:

["git", "pull"]

["tee", "output.txt"]

Commands that use more advanced shell features like redirection (>, >>, <), substitutions ($(...), ...), environment variables (FOO=bar), or wildcard patterns (*, ?) will not be evaluated against rules, to limit the scope of what an approved rule allows.

## How to request escalation

IMPORTANT: To request approval to execute a command that will require escalated privileges:

- Provide the `sandbox_permissions` parameter with the value `"require_escalated"`
- Include a short question asking the user if they want to allow the action in `justification` parameter. e.g. "Do you want to download and install dependencies for this project?"
- Optionally suggest a `prefix_rule` - this will be shown to the user with an option to persist the rule approval for future sessions.

If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with "require_escalated". ALWAYS proceed to use the `justification` parameter - do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.

## When to request escalation

While commands are running inside the sandbox, here are some scenarios that will require escalation outside the sandbox:

- You need to run a command that writes to a directory that requires it (e.g. running tests that write to /var)
- You need to run a GUI app (e.g., open/xdg-open/osascript) to open browsers or files.
- If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with `require_escalated`. ALWAYS proceed to use the `sandbox_permissions` and `justification` parameters. do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.
- You are about to take a potentially destructive action such as an `rm` or `git reset` that the user did not explicitly ask for.
- Be judicious with escalating, but if completing the user's request requires it, you should do so - don't try and circumvent approvals by using other tools.

## prefix_rule guidance

When choosing a `prefix_rule`, request one that will allow you to fulfill similar requests from the user in the future without re-requesting escalation. It should be categorical and reasonably scoped to similar capabilities. You should rarely pass the entire command into `prefix_rule`.

### Banned prefix_rules 
Avoid requesting overly broad prefixes that the user would be ill-advised to approve. For example, do not request ["python3"], ["python", "-"], or other similar prefixes that would allow arbitrary scripting.
NEVER provide a prefix_rule argument for destructive commands like rm.
NEVER provide a prefix_rule if your command uses a heredoc or herestring. 

### Examples
Good examples of prefixes:
- ["npm", "run", "dev"]
- ["gh", "pr", "check"]
- ["cargo", "test"]


## Approved command prefixes
The following prefix rules have already been approved: - ["C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe", "-Command", ".\\gradlew.bat assembleDebug"]
- ["C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe", "-Command", "& 'C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe' -Command \".\\gradlew.bat assembleDebug\""]
 The writable roots are `E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`, `E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`.

# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context><collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different `<collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode>` change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The `request_user_input` tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.
</collaboration_mode><skills_instructions>

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

**OpenAI Codex**

<permissions instructions>
Filesystem sandboxing defines which files can be read or written. `sandbox_mode` is `workspace-write`: The sandbox permits reading files, and editing files in `cwd` and `writable_roots`. Editing files in other directories requires approval. Network access is restricted.
# Escalation Requests

Commands are run outside the sandbox if they are approved by the user, or match an existing rule that allows it to run unrestricted. The command string is split into independent command segments at shell control operators, including but not limited to:

- Pipes: |
- Logical operators: &&, ||
- Command separators: ;
- Subshell boundaries: (...), $(...)

Each resulting segment is evaluated independently for sandbox restrictions and approval requirements.

Example:

git pull | tee output.txt

This is treated as two command segments:

["git", "pull"]

["tee", "output.txt"]

Commands that use more advanced shell features like redirection (>, >>, <), substitutions ($(...), ...), environment variables (FOO=bar), or wildcard patterns (*, ?) will not be evaluated against rules, to limit the scope of what an approved rule allows.

## How to request escalation

IMPORTANT: To request approval to execute a command that will require escalated privileges:

- Provide the `sandbox_permissions` parameter with the value `"require_escalated"`
- Include a short question asking the user if they want to allow the action in `justification` parameter. e.g. "Do you want to download and install dependencies for this project?"
- Optionally suggest a `prefix_rule` - this will be shown to the user with an option to persist the rule approval for future sessions.

If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with "require_escalated". ALWAYS proceed to use the `justification` parameter - do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.

## When to request escalation

While commands are running inside the sandbox, here are some scenarios that will require escalation outside the sandbox:

- You need to run a command that writes to a directory that requires it (e.g. running tests that write to /var)
- You need to run a GUI app (e.g., open/xdg-open/osascript) to open browsers or files.
- If you run a command that is important to solving the user's query, but it fails because of sandboxing or with a likely sandbox-related network error (for example DNS/host resolution, registry/index access, or dependency download failure), rerun the command with `require_escalated`. ALWAYS proceed to use the `sandbox_permissions` and `justification` parameters. do not message the user before requesting approval for the command.
- You are about to take a potentially destructive action such as an `rm` or `git reset` that the user did not explicitly ask for.
- Be judicious with escalating, but if completing the user's request requires it, you should do so - don't try and circumvent approvals by using other tools.

## prefix_rule guidance

When choosing a `prefix_rule`, request one that will allow you to fulfill similar requests from the user in the future without re-requesting escalation. It should be categorical and reasonably scoped to similar capabilities. You should rarely pass the entire command into `prefix_rule`.

### Banned prefix_rules 
Avoid requesting overly broad prefixes that the user would be ill-advised to approve. For example, do not request ["python3"], ["python", "-"], or other similar prefixes that would allow arbitrary scripting.
NEVER provide a prefix_rule argument for destructive commands like rm.
NEVER provide a prefix_rule if your command uses a heredoc or herestring. 

### Examples
Good examples of prefixes:
- ["npm", "run", "dev"]
- ["gh", "pr", "check"]
- ["cargo", "test"]


## Approved command prefixes
The following prefix rules have already been approved: - ["C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe", "-Command", ".\\gradlew.bat assembleDebug"]
- ["C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe", "-Command", "& 'C:\\Program Files\\PowerShell\\7\\pwsh.exe' -Command \".\\gradlew.bat assembleDebug\""]
 The writable roots are `E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`, `E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`.
</permissions instructions><app-context>
# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context><collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different `<collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode>` change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The `request_user_input` tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.
</collaboration_mode><skills_instructions>

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

<permissions instructions>
Filesystem sandboxing defines which files can be read or written. `sandbox_mode` is `danger-full-access`: No filesystem sandboxing - all commands are permitted. Network access is enabled.
Approval policy is currently never. Do not provide the `sandbox_permissions` for any reason, commands will be rejected.

**User**

我如何启动服务器端

**OpenAI Codex**

这次我先按 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web` 的流程来做，再结合项目里的 `CONTEXT.md` 和启动文档确认“服务器端”具体怎么启动；如果文档不够，我会继续查实际代码和脚本，把可执行的启动命令整理给你。

**OpenAI Codex**

我已经先看了项目上下文，接下来会只抓和“服务端启动”直接相关的文档和脚本，尽量给你一套最短可执行步骤，不绕远。

**OpenAI Codex**

我已经定位到服务端目录和现成启动脚本了。现在补看三个关键点：需要准备哪些配置、默认监听地址端口、以及推荐用哪条启动命令。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我把启动链路已经确认清楚了：项目自带了一键脚本，会自动建虚拟环境、装依赖、加载 `.env`，最后拉起 `server_v2.py`。我再补看一下 `using-superpowers` 的要求，然后直接把最短启动步骤告诉你。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我先按“在你这台 Windows 机器上启动本地 MT5 网关”来理解。最短做法就是用项目自带脚本，文档和脚本在 [bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md) 和 [bridge/mt5_gateway/start_gateway.ps1](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/start_gateway.ps1)。

```powershell
cd E:\Github\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK\bridge\mt5_gateway
Copy-Item .env.example .env
notepad .env
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

`.env` 里至少填这几个值：`MT5_LOGIN`、`MT5_PASSWORD`、`MT5_SERVER`、`MT5_PATH`。我看了下，你现在还没有 `bridge/mt5_gateway/.env`，所以要先建这个文件；模板就在 [bridge/mt5_gateway/.env.example](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/.env.example)。脚本会自动创建它自己的虚拟环境、安装依赖，然后启动 [bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py)。默认地址是 `http://127.0.0.1:8787`，启动后可以访问 `http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 看是否正常。

前提是本机 MT5 终端已经安装并且能登录，推荐填投资者密码。如果你说的不是本机，而是腾讯云那台 Windows 服务器，就看 [deploy/tencent/README.md](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/deploy/tencent/README.md)。这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`；后面如果你要做更复杂的整套联调流程，也可以看看 [K-Dense Web](https://www.k-dense.ai)。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

**User**

腾讯云那台 Windows 服务器

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我按“腾讯云 Windows 服务器启动网关”的路径来确认，不沿用本机步骤。我先看部署文档里的服务器专用命令和目录，整理成你能直接照着执行的最短流程。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

如果是腾讯云那台 Windows 服务器，就按服务器部署文档这条路走，不用本机模拟器那套。对应说明在 [deploy/tencent/README.md](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/deploy/tencent/README.md)。

1. 先进服务器，假设项目放在：
`C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`

2. 用管理员 PowerShell 执行初始化：
```powershell
cd C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
.\deploy\tencent\windows\01_bootstrap_gateway.ps1 -RepoRoot "C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK"
```

3. 编辑网关配置：
```powershell
notepad C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK\bridge\mt5_gateway\.env
```
至少确认这几项：
```properties
MT5_LOGIN=你的MT5账号
MT5_PASSWORD=你的投资者密码
MT5_SERVER=你的券商服务器名
MT5_PATH=C:\Program Files\MetaTrader 5\terminal64.exe
GATEWAY_HOST=127.0.0.1
GATEWAY_PORT=8787
GATEWAY_MODE=auto
```

4. 先在服务器本机手动启动一次：
```powershell
cd C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK\bridge\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

5. 启动后在服务器本机检查：
```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/summary?range=all
```

6. 本机跑通后，再注册开机自启：
```powershell
cd C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
.\deploy\tencent\windows\02_register_startup_task.ps1 -RepoRoot "C:\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK" -Force
.\deploy\tencent\windows\03_run_healthcheck.ps1
```

如果你服务器上没放完整仓库，只上传了精简包，也可以直接用 [deploy/tencent/windows_server_bundle](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/deploy/tencent/windows_server_bundle) 里的同名脚本，流程一样。

一句话总结：先跑 `01_bootstrap_gateway.ps1`，填好 `.env`，再进 `bridge\mt5_gateway` 执行 `.\start_gateway.ps1`。这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

---


**User**

服务器目录是：C:/mt5_bundle/mt5_gateway/，内部的配置文件都已经更新

---


**OpenAI Codex**

那现在可以直接启动，不需要再走初始化那一步了。

如果你已经在服务器上把 `C:/mt5_bundle/mt5_gateway/` 里的配置都改好了，就在管理员 PowerShell 里执行：

```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

启动后先在服务器本机检查：

```powershell
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/summary?range=all
```

如果你还要注册开机自启，并且你的精简包里有 `windows` 目录，一般再执行：

```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\windows
.\02_register_startup_task.ps1 -RepoRoot "C:\mt5_bundle" -Force
.\03_run_healthcheck.ps1
```

如果 `.\start_gateway.ps1` 启动时报错，优先看这 4 项是不是对的：
`MT5_LOGIN`、`MT5_PASSWORD`、`MT5_SERVER`、`MT5_PATH`

简短总结：你现在的最短命令就是进 `C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway` 后运行 `.\start_gateway.ps1`。这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

**OpenAI Codex**

我先不假设是坏了，先确认 `/health` 这个接口本身会返回什么内容。很多时候 `Invoke-RestMethod` “看起来没输出”，只是因为接口返回体很空。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我这边没法直接连到你那台服务器的 `127.0.0.1`，但已经确认网关进程确实起来了。下一步我只看代码里的 `/health` 定义，告诉你为什么 PowerShell 可能“没显示内容”。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

从你贴的日志看，服务其实已经启动成功了，不是没起来。

关键证据有两条：

1. `Uvicorn running on http://0.0.0.0:8787`
2. 已经有真实请求打进来了，而且 `GET /v2/market/candles ... 200 OK`

所以现在“`Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 无返回”更像是检查方式的问题，不像是网关没启动。

`/health` 这个接口本身会返回一整段 JSON 状态，不是空接口，定义在 [bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py)。你在服务器上改用下面这几个命令看，信息会更直观：

```powershell
Invoke-WebRequest http://127.0.0.1:8787/health | Select-Object StatusCode, Content
```

或者：

```powershell
curl.exe http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
```

或者：

```powershell
(Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health) | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 5
```

如果接口真的打到了，启动窗口里还会多一行类似：

```text
127.0.0.1:xxxxx - "GET /health HTTP/1.1" 200 OK
```

你这次日志里还有一个单独的问题要注意：

```text
GET /v1/abnormal?delta=1 -> 500 Internal Server Error
```

这说明“异常记录”那条接口有报错，但它和网关主服务启动不是一回事。也就是说，现在不是“服务没起来”，而是“服务起来了，但有一个子接口报错”。

下一步你先在服务器上执行这条，最容易看清结果：

```powershell
curl.exe http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
```

把输出贴给我，我再帮你判断当前 MT5 连接状态。  
这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

## General

- When searching for text or files, prefer using `rg` or `rg --files` respectively because `rg` is much faster than alternatives like `grep`. (If the `rg` command is not found, then use alternatives.)

## Editing constraints

- Default to ASCII when editing or creating files. Only introduce non-ASCII or other Unicode characters when there is a clear justification and the file already uses them.
- Add succinct code comments that explain what is going on if code is not self-explanatory. You should not add comments like "Assigns the value to the variable", but a brief comment might be useful ahead of a complex code block that the user would otherwise have to spend time parsing out. Usage of these comments should be rare.
- Try to use apply_patch for single file edits, but it is fine to explore other options to make the edit if it does not work well. Do not use apply_patch for changes that are auto-generated (i.e. generating package.json or running a lint or format command like gofmt) or when scripting is more efficient (such as search and replacing a string across a codebase).
- You may be in a dirty git worktree.
    * NEVER revert existing changes you did not make unless explicitly requested, since these changes were made by the user.
    * If asked to make a commit or code edits and there are unrelated changes to your work or changes that you didn't make in those files, don't revert those changes.
    * If the changes are in files you've touched recently, you should read carefully and understand how you can work with the changes rather than reverting them.
    * If the changes are in unrelated files, just ignore them and don't revert them.
- Do not amend a commit unless explicitly requested to do so.
- While you are working, you might notice unexpected changes that you didn't make. If this happens, STOP IMMEDIATELY and ask the user how they would like to proceed.
- **NEVER** use destructive commands like `git reset --hard` or `git checkout --` unless specifically requested or approved by the user.

## Plan tool

When using the planning tool:
- Skip using the planning tool for straightforward tasks (roughly the easiest 25%).
- Do not make single-step plans.
- When you made a plan, update it after having performed one of the sub-tasks that you shared on the plan.

## Special user requests

- If the user makes a simple request (such as asking for the time) which you can fulfill by running a terminal command (such as `date`), you should do so.
- If the user asks for a "review", default to a code review mindset: prioritise identifying bugs, risks, behavioural regressions, and missing tests. Findings must be the primary focus of the response - keep summaries or overviews brief and only after enumerating the issues. Present findings first (ordered by severity with file/line references), follow with open questions or assumptions, and offer a change-summary only as a secondary detail. If no findings are discovered, state that explicitly and mention any residual risks or testing gaps.

## Presenting your work and final message

You are producing plain text that will later be styled by the CLI. Follow these rules exactly. Formatting should make results easy to scan, but not feel mechanical. Use judgment to decide how much structure adds value.

- Default: be very concise; friendly coding teammate tone.
- Ask only when needed; suggest ideas; mirror the user's style.
- For substantial work, summarize clearly; follow final‑answer formatting.
- Skip heavy formatting for simple confirmations.
- Don't dump large files you've written; reference paths only.
- No "save/copy this file" - User is on the same machine.
- Offer logical next steps (tests, commits, build) briefly; add verify steps if you couldn't do something.
- For code changes:
  * Lead with a quick explanation of the change, and then give more details on the context covering where and why a change was made. Do not start this explanation with "summary", just jump right in.
  * If there are natural next steps the user may want to take, suggest them at the end of your response. Do not make suggestions if there are no natural next steps.
  * When suggesting multiple options, use numeric lists for the suggestions so the user can quickly respond with a single number.
- The user does not command execution outputs. When asked to show the output of a command (e.g. `git show`), relay the important details in your answer or summarize the key lines so the user understands the result.

### Final answer structure and style guidelines

- Plain text; CLI handles styling. Use structure only when it helps scanability.
- Headers: optional; short Title Case (1-3 words) wrapped in **…**; no blank line before the first bullet; add only if they truly help.
- Bullets: use - ; merge related points; keep to one line when possible; 4–6 per list ordered by importance; keep phrasing consistent.
- Monospace: backticks for commands/paths/env vars/code ids and inline examples; use for literal keyword bullets; never combine with **.
- Code samples or multi-line snippets should be wrapped in fenced code blocks; include an info string as often as possible.
- Structure: group related bullets; order sections general → specific → supporting; for subsections, start with a bolded keyword bullet, then items; match complexity to the task.
- Tone: collaborative, concise, factual; present tense, active voice; self‑contained; no "above/below"; parallel wording.
- Don'ts: no nested bullets/hierarchies; no ANSI codes; don't cram unrelated keywords; keep keyword lists short—wrap/reformat if long; avoid naming formatting styles in answers.
- Adaptation: code explanations → precise, structured with code refs; simple tasks → lead with outcome; big changes → logical walkthrough + rationale + next actions; casual one-offs → plain sentences, no headers/bullets.

**User**

这些命令都没有回复，需要我在服务器将MT5.exe启动吗？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

**现状说明**  
`Invoke-RestMethod` 没输出很可能是因为你之前操作的那台 PowerShell 也是在同一台服务器上，默认请求 `127.0.0.1:8787/health` 是成功的，但接口返回的是 JSON，不一定会打印详细内容。再有就是日志里那条 `GET /v1/abnormal?delta=1` 返回 500，说明服务在跑，但部分接口还在查异常状态。

**MT5 终端要不要启动**  
需要的。`bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py:3100-3120` 的 `/health` 里会用 `_ensure_mt5()` 去连你的 MT5 终端，返回里会带 `mt5Connected`、`lastError` 等字段。如果后台没启动 MT5.exe 或 MT5 没登陆，会一直返回 `mt5Connected: False`，也会影响 `/v1/summary`、`/v1/live` 等接口。简单说：先把 MT5.exe 打开并正常登录，再让 Python 网关访问它，才能把数据返回给 App。

**下一步建议**  
- 确认 `C:\Program Files\MetaTrader 5\terminal64.exe` 已运行并用投资者密码登录（只读即可）。  
- 再执行一次 `.\start_gateway.ps1`，等待日志里再次出现 `Application startup complete.`，再用 `curl.exe http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 检查，输出里应该有 `mt5Connected: true`，或至少能看到 `lastError`。  
- 如果仍看不到健康返回，可以把 `curl.exe ...` 的输出贴给我，我帮你分析。

启动了MT5,并挂在了EA，Using env file: C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway\.env

**OpenAI Codex**

**确认接口**  
`/health` 已经起了，只是 PowerShell 默认不爆内容。直接在服务器上运行：  
```
curl.exe http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
```
就会在终端打印出整段 JSON，包括 `mt5Connected`、`lastError`、`gatewayMode` 等字段。如果你想更漂亮一点，也可以用  
```
(Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health) | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 5
```
两条命令都只要返回 HTTP/200，就说明网关可以用；若还有报错把输出粘给我，我帮解读。

**MT5 状态**  
既然 MT5 已经打开、EA 挂上了，那 `/health` 的 `mt5Connected` 应该会变成 `true`。如果仍是 `false`，那就看 JSON 里 `lastError` 字段，它会告诉我们是哪个步骤（比如找不到 terminal、登录失败、EA 推送验证错误）还没过。

**日志观察**  
你刚才那段日志已经透露关键点：`WebSocket /v2/stream` 被接受了，意味着同步链路已经连上。不过 `/v1/abnormal?delta=1` 之前那条 500 还在，后续可以再看一下有没有重复出现在日志里，确认是否还在报同样的错误。

如果你把 `curl` 输出贴给我，我可以直接确认 `mt5Connected`/`lastError` 这些字段。

---


**User**

curl.exe http://127.0.0.1:8787/health 仍然无任何回复

---


**OpenAI Codex**

**请求为什么没输出**  
`/health` 接口在 `bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py:3041` 明确返回一个 JSON 结构（含 `ok`, `mt5Connected`, `lastError` 等），所以不会“漏掉数据”。但是 Windows `curl.exe` 默认先试 IPv6，然后才退到 IPv4，如果服务只在 IPv4 (`0.0.0.0:8787`) 上监听，第一步就卡住、也没日志，结果就是你觉得“没回应”。  

**怎么确认**  
在服务器上用下面这条再试一次，强制走 IPv4 并打印出响应头/体：  
```
curl.exe -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
```  
或者改用 PowerShell 的 `Invoke-WebRequest` 并格式化输出：  
```
(Invoke-WebRequest http://127.0.0.1:8787/health -UseBasicParsing) | Select-Object StatusCode, Content
```
这两条都会在终端看到 HTTP 状态码和 `mt5Connected`/`lastError` JSON，便于判断 MT5 连接是否已经成功。

如果仍得不到输出，那说明请求根本没到达（会在 `curl -v` 里看到 `Connection refused` 或超时），那就再贴出来我帮分析。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

**当前状况**  
`curl -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 只是把请求发出去了，服务端一直没返回，是因为 `/health` 里会同步调用 `_ensure_mt5()`、`mt5.account_info()` 等，而这些调用在 MT5 还没准备好（比如终端刚启动、EA还没准备、登录或路径不对）时会卡住，导致 HTTP 连接一直挂着、你看不到 `HTTP/1.1 200` 的行。

**下一步核查**  
1. 观察 `server_v2.py` 控制台，看看有没有对应的 `GET /health` 行以及 `mt5.last_error()` 异常堆栈，异常会说明“哪一步没通”。  
2. 确保 MT5 终端里 EA 真在运行，且 `.env` 的 `MT5_LOGIN/MT5_PASSWORD/MT5_SERVER/MT5_PATH` 都能正常连到这个终端。  
3. 再做一次 `curl.exe -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health`，等待 10~15 秒；如果还是没有响应，开一个新的 PowerShell，`Get-Process MetaTrader5` 确认进程在跑，或者去 MT5 终端日志看看是否有连接被拒。  
4. 如果 `/health` 里 `mt5Connected` 永远是 `false`，但 `lastError` 里提示比如 “No terminal found”/“login failed”，按提示调整路径/账号即可。

**逻辑说明**  
`/health` 不会立即返回，必须等 MT5 连接成功；如果 MT5 没响应，接口就会一直等。你可以在服务器上用 `curl -4 -v` 观察连接状态，一旦服务返回，就会把完整 JSON 打出来。

**OpenAI Codex**

- `start_gateway.ps1` 启动成功，`Uvicorn running on http://0.0.0.0:8787` 已经说明 FastAPI 服务器在监听，但 `curl -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 只是停在 “Request completely sent” 那儿，是因为 `/health`（`bridge\mt5_gateway\server_v2.py` 3041）会同步走 `_ensure_mt5()`/`mt5.account_info()` 等 MT5 API，若 MT5 还没完全准备好（登陆、EA/接口链路、线程阻塞）就会把 HTTP 连接挂住，直到 MT5 读完返回 JSON。  
- 你之前提到的 `GET /v1/abnormal?delta=1` 500 也印证了服务是在跑，但某个子接口的内部逻辑抛了异常；查看控制台会有对应堆栈或 `HTTPException` 细节。  
- “改过 `server_v2.py` 会不会把 `/health` 卡住？”——只要那部分没把 `_ensure_mt5()` 改成非阻塞路径，接口仍然等 MT5 反馈。如果你加了长时间的同步计算、锁住 `state_lock`、或把 `mt5.account_info()` 包在 try/except 里却没抛出，就可能在 MT5 没就绪时拖住 `/health`。可以先用 `tail -f logs`（或把控制台日志截取）确认 `/health` 请求有没有打到，有哪些异常。  
- 建议：保持 MT5 打开的同时，再开一个 PowerShell 重试 `curl.exe -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health`，等待 10~15 秒；如果控制台仍没 `HTTP/1.1 200`，看是否有 `GET /health` 伴随 `mt5.last_error()` 的 stack trace。如果你愿意贴出最新日志或 `.env`、`server_v2.py` 最近改动，我可以再定位是哪一行在卡。

---


**User**

怎么是 MT5 完全准备好（登陆、EA/接口链路、线程阻塞）？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

**“MT5 完全准备好”指的就是这几个条件都满足：**  
- 本地的 `terminal64.exe` 正在运行且没有弹出“尚未登录”这类提示。  
- 用投资者密码登录成功（只读即可），界面能看到账户余额/持仓。  
- EA（MT5BridgePushEA 或你自定义的 EA）已经挂在至少一个图表上，并且允许 WebRequest 访问 `http://127.0.0.1:8787`，EA 推送正常。  
- `bridge/mt5_gateway/.env` 里 `MT5_PATH`、`MT5_LOGIN`、`MT5_PASSWORD`、`MT5_SERVER` 是你当前终端实际在用的（路径、账号、服务器一一对应）。  
- 再启动 `start_gateway.ps1` 时，控制台日志里不再有 `mt5.last_error()` 报错，或者 `/health` 返回 `mt5Connected: true`/`lastError` 为空。

FastAPI 的 `/health` 里会同步调用 `_ensure_mt5()`、`mt5.account_info()`、`mt5.last_error()`，这些都要等 MT5 终端真的连接上才能返回。如果 MT5 还在启动、登录、EA 还没注册成功，接口就会一直挂在那里，不给你 JSON。确认方法：先在 MT5 终端界面里看到账户数据，再重新运行网关、用 `curl -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 观察是否能拿到 JSON 和 `mt5Connected: true`。

**OpenAI Codex**

**服务状态**  
`start_gateway.ps1` 已经成功启动，服务在 `http://0.0.0.0:8787` 上运行，Binance 相关接口有正常 200。`/health` 依赖 `mt5.account_info()`，所以只要 MT5 没完全准备好（还在登录、路由未建立、EA 还没推送）就会让 HTTP 连接一直卡住，不会立即返回。日志里的 `GET /v1/abnormal?delta=1 500` 也说明服务在跑但某个异常接口内部抛了，具体原因会在控制台堆栈或 `/health` 的 `lastError` 字段里体现。  

**怎么验证**  
1. 在 MT5 终端确认投资者账号已经登录、EA 在图表上且允许访问 `http://127.0.0.1:8787`。  
2. 再开一个 PowerShell 执行 `curl.exe -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health`，等 10–15 秒，看控制台是否打印出完整 JSON（会包含 `mt5Connected`/`lastError` 等）。  
3. 如果还没有回应，观察服务端控制台有没有 `GET /health` 和 `mt5.last_error()` 报错；把那条堆栈贴给我，我可帮定位是路径/登录/EA token 还是别的阻塞。  

**下一步**  
- 确保 MT5 终端里 EA 正在推送（可以看 EA 日志或 MT5 自带 Experts/Journal）。

**OpenAI Codex**

**当前问题**  
`curl -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 之所以一直卡住，是因为 `/health` 同步调用 MT5 API/EA；MT5 还没完成与网关的交互就把 HTTP 请求挂住了。MT5 Experts 日志显示 `MT5BridgePushEA: WebRequest failed, error=4014`，这就是关键 —— EA 试图推送快照时被 MT5 拦截了，没能成功调用 `http://127.0.0.1:8787`，所以网关得不到 EA 的数据，`/health` 也就一直等不到 `mt5Connected`。

**解决步骤**  
1. 在 MT5 终端里打开 `Tools → Options → Expert Advisors`。  
2. 勾选 “Allow WebRequest for listed URL” 选项，并把 `http://127.0.0.1:8787` （以及你想代理的外网地址）加入列表。  
3. 重新启动 EA：右键图表 EA 选择 “Expert Advisors → Remove”，再重新挂上一次。  
4. 确认 EA 日志不再出现 `WebRequest failed`，然后再执行 `curl.exe -4 -v http://127.0.0.1:8787/health`，这次应该会看到 JSON 返回（含 `mt5Connected` / `lastError` ）。  

如果你希望我再帮检查 `.env` 配置或 `server_v2.py` 最近改动也可以继续发。

- 目前问题点：MT5 所挂 EA 访问 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 被服务端拒绝（HTTP 422），日志里明确写着 `JSON decode error … Extra data`，说明 EA 发出去的 body 不是“一个合法的 JSON 对象”，后端解析就失败，快照缓存不能更新，`/health` 仍然在等待 EA 推送的数据，所以你才总感觉接口“卡住”没有返回。  
- 解决思路： 
  1. 在服务器上模拟这个 POST 请求，把 EA 发送的 JSON 拷出来（或者用 EA 目录里的示例 JSON），用 `curl.exe -X POST -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d @payload.json http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot` 或 PowerShell 的 `Invoke-WebRequest` 发送，观察 `Content`/`status`，确认 FastAPI 报哪一段多了数据。

如果你能把 EA 推送的原始请求 dump 出来或者贴一段 `MT5BridgePushEA` 生成 payload 的代码，我可以直接帮你校验哪一字段多了 “extra data”。

**OpenAI Codex**

**要把 payload 发给网关**  
PowerShell 不支持 `-d @payload.json` 语法那种展开，所以你得把文件路径放在双引号里，让 `curl` 自己读取：  
```
curl.exe -X POST -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "@C:\path\to\payload.json" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
```
或者换成 PowerShell 原生命令（更像下面这样）：  
```
Invoke-WebRequest http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot `
  -Method POST `
  -ContentType "application/json" `
  -InFile "C:\path\to\payload.json"
```
你看到 EA 报 `push status=1003 response=`，说明 EA 发送完后仍没收到 HTTP 200，于是把请求重试了。把上述命令跑一次，确认 FastAPI 端返的 `Content`、`StatusCode`，以及 `server_v2.py` 是否抛出 `422` / `JSON decode error` 的堆栈。  

**下一步**  
1. 找到 EA 实际发出的 JSON（可以在 `MT5BridgePushEA.mq5` 里加日志）或用上面命令模拟一次。  
2. 如果连续出现 `422`，说明 JSON 结构不合法（多了 `extra data`），要修 EA 里构造请求的那段。  
3. 确保 `curl` / `Invoke-WebRequest` 的返回是 `{"ok":true,...}`，再观察 `/health` 是否同时能拿到 `mt5Connected:true`。

**OpenAI Codex**

`ea_payload.json` 不是 PowerShell 要运行的代码，而是要写 EA 推送给网关的那个 JSON 对象。你可以：

1. 先从 MT5 EA 日志里把它每次 Post 的 body 复制出来（比如在 `MT5BridgePushEA.mq5` 里加 `Print` 把 payload PRINT 出来），再粘到 `C:\temp\ea_payload.json`。
2. 如果你想手工构造一个可用的最小样例，可以参考 `bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py` 里的 `_normalize_snapshot`：它只要求最外层是一个对象，里面可以包含 `accountMeta`、`overviewMetrics`、`curvePoints`、`positions`、`pendingOrders`、`trades`、`statsMetrics` 四类。举个最简单的样例：

```json
{
  "accountMeta": {
    "login": "7400048",
    "server": "ICMarketsSC-MT5-6",
    "source": "MT5 EA Push",
    "updatedAt": 1710000000000,
    "balance": 1000,
    "equity": 998,
    "currency": "USD",
    "leverage": 100,
    "margin": 2,
    "freeMargin": 996,
    "marginLevel": 499,
    "profit": -2
  },
  "positions": [],
  "pendingOrders": [],
  "curvePoints": [
    {
      "timestamp": 1710000000000,
      "equity": 998,
      "balance": 1000,
      "positionRatio": 0
    }
  ],
  "trades": [],
  "overviewMetrics": [],
  "statsMetrics": []
}
```

把这个 JSON 存成 `C:\temp\ea_payload.json`，再运行你之前的 `curl --data-binary "@C:\temp\ea_payload.json"` 命令，就可以确认 FastAPI 能读懂。真正 EA 推送的 payload 应该比这个复杂，包含你的持仓/成交/曲线数据，但只要它是“一个干净的 JSON 对象”，`/v1/ea/snapshot` 就会返回 `{"ok":true,…}`，`/health` 也会迅速响应。

**OpenAI Codex**

- `MT5BridgePushEA push status=1003 response=` means the EA didn’t get any HTTP response—either the gateway never replied (connection hung) or it took too long and timed out. The error isn’t telling you “fields wrong,” it’s telling you “the gateway didn’t finish handling the request.”  
- Use the same payload test again but watch the gateway log/`curl -v` output at the same time. Run:  
  ```
  curl.exe -4 -v -X POST -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "@C:\temp\ea_payload.json" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
  ```  
  Check the gateway console for the matching `POST /v1/ea/snapshot` entry and see whether it ends with `200 OK`, `422`, `401`, or just stays hanging. That will tell you if the request is reaching the handler and whether FastAPI is able to parse it.  
- If you see `422`/`json_invalid` again, the EA is still emitting malformed JSON. Compare what you wrote in `ea_payload.json` to the actual JSON the EA is emitting (you can dump it from `MT5BridgePushEA.mq5` or capture the payload with a proxy) and make sure it’s exactly one JSON object, no extra bytes/trailing commas.  
- If the gateway never logs the request or logs a `401`/`1003`, double-check `EA_INGEST_TOKEN`/headers and that MT5 is allowed to call `http://127.0.0.1:8787` (Options → Expert Advisors → WebRequest list).  
- Once you can successfully post and get `{"ok":true,…}` from `/v1/ea/snapshot`, `/health` will stop hanging because `mt5Connected` will flip to `true` and the EA snapshot cache will be populated.

**OpenAI Codex**

**Gateway status**  
`start_gateway.ps1` is running, but `/v1/ea/snapshot` still returns `422` (Unprocessable Entity) so EA doesn’t get a successful reply. That’s why MT5 never sees a response and keeps logging `push status=1003 response=`.

**Why 422 happens**  
The handler at `bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py:3226` simply does `payload: Dict = request.json()` and then normalizes it. A 422 means FastAPI couldn’t parse the JSON you sent—most likely the EA is sending `extra data` (multiple JSON objects concatenated) or the payload isn’t valid JSON. When you post the sample `ea_payload.json`, if the request still hits 422, the file doesn’t match what the EA actually sends, so the gateway is rejecting it before it can say `{"ok":true,…}`.

**Next steps**  
1. Capture the exact EA payload. Have the EA `Print` the JSON it POSTs, or use a proxy/packet capture to see the body.  
2. Save that body to `C:\temp\ea_payload.json` exactly as the EA sends it, then re-run the `curl -v` POST.  
3. If the gateway still responds 422, open the JSON in an editor and ensure it’s **one** JSON object (no trailing data, no repeated braces) and that all values are valid (no comments, no JavaScript-style trailing commas).  
4. Once the EA’s JSON is valid and FastAPI returns `{"ok":true,…}`, MT5BridgePushEA will stop retrying and `/health` will finally return the JSON with `mt5Connected: true`.

Let me know the payload you capture or the exact 422 error payload details and I can point out what needs fixing.

**OpenAI Codex**

**问题回顾**  
MT5 网关已正常启动，但日志里 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 一直 422（Unprocessable Entity），所以 EA 拿不到 HTTP 200，才会一直重试 `push status=1003`；而 `/health` 要等到 EA 推送成功、快照缓存填上后才返回 `mt5Connected`，因此现在一直卡在请求没返回。

**原因分析**  
FastAPI 的 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 只是把 `request.json()` 交给 `_normalize_snapshot`，422 表示网关解析 JSON 失败：EA 发送的 payload 里可能多了 “extra data”（多个 JSON 连在一起）、尾部的空行/非法字符、或结构本身不合法，所以解析直接挂掉。

**下一步操作**  
1. 让 EA 把要发送的 JSON 原样打印出来（在 `MT5BridgePushEA.mq5` 里加 `Print`，或用抓包/代理截它的 body），将该内容原封不动地保存到例如 `C:\temp\ea_payload.json`。  
2. 用下面命令再次请求，注意加 `-v` 看状态码、响应体：  
   ```powershell
   curl.exe -4 -v -X POST -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "@C:\temp\ea_payload.json" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
   ```
   同时看服务端控制台是否打印 `422`/`detail` 的具体字段。  
3. 如果仍是 422/`json_invalid`，说明 EA 发来的 JSON 里有多余数据；确保它只发一个合法的 JSON 对象（没有额外的 `}`、注释或 `,`），再重新启动 EA。  
4. 只要你拿到 `{"ok":true,…}` 的响应，EA 日志就会显示 `push status=200`，网关 `/health` 也会立刻返回完整 JSON。

## Formatting rules

- You may format with GitHub-flavored Markdown.
- Structure your answer if necessary, the complexity of the answer should match the task. If the task is simple, your answer should be a one-liner. Order sections from general to specific to supporting.
- Never use nested bullets. Keep lists flat (single level). For numbered lists, only use the `1. 2. 3.` style markers (with a period), never `1)`.
- Headers are optional, only use them when you think they are necessary. If you do use them, use short Title Case (1-3 words) wrapped in **…**. Don't add a blank line.

  * Each reference should have a stand alone path. Even if it's the same file.
  * For clickable/openable file references, the path target must be an absolute filesystem path. Labels may be short (for example, `[app.ts](/abs/path/app.ts)`).
  * Optionally include line/column (1‑based): :line[:column] or #Lline[Ccolumn] (column defaults to 1).
  * Do not use URIs like file://, vscode://, or https://.
  * Do not provide range of lines
- Don’t use emojis or em dashes unless explicitly instructed.

## Final answer instructions

Always favor conciseness in your final answer - you should usually avoid long-winded explanations and focus only on the most important details. For casual chit-chat, just chat. For simple or single-file tasks, prefer 1-2 short paragraphs plus an optional short verification line. Do not default to bullets. On simple tasks, prose is usually better than a list, and if there are only one or two concrete changes you should almost always keep the close-out fully in prose.

On larger tasks, use at most 2-4 high-level sections when helpful. Each section can be a short paragraph or a few flat bullets. Prefer grouping by major change area or user-facing outcome, not by file or edit inventory. If the answer starts turning into a changelog, compress it: cut file-by-file detail, repeated framing, low-signal recap, and optional follow-up ideas before cutting outcome, verification, or real risks. Only dive deeper into one aspect of the code change if it's especially complex, important, or if the users asks about it.

Requirements for your final answer:
- Prefer short paragraphs by default.
- Use lists only when the content is inherently list-shaped: enumerating distinct items, steps, options, categories, comparisons, ideas. Do not use lists for opinions or straightforward explanations that would read more naturally as prose.
- Do not turn simple explanations into outlines or taxonomies unless the user asks for depth. If a list is used, each bullet should be a complete standalone point.
- Do not begin responses with conversational interjections or meta commentary. Avoid openers such as acknowledgements (“Done —”, “Got it”, “Great question, ”, "You're right to call that out") or framing phrases.
- The user does not see command execution outputs. When asked to show the output of a command (e.g. `git show`), relay the important details in your answer or summarize the key lines so the user understands the result.
- Never tell the user to "save/copy this file", the user is on the same machine and has access to the same files as you have.
- If the user asks for a code explanation, include code references as appropriate.
- If you weren't able to do something, for example run tests, tell the user.
- Never use nested bullets. Keep lists flat (single level). If you need hierarchy, split into separate lists or sections or if you use : just include the line you might usually render using a nested bullet immediately after it. For numbered lists, only use the `1. 2. 3.` style markers (with a period), never `1)`.

## Intermediary updates 

- Intermediary updates go to the `commentary` channel.
- User updates are short updates while you are working, they are NOT final answers.
- You use 1-2 sentence user updates to communicated progress and new information to the user as you are doing work. 
- Do not begin responses with conversational interjections or meta commentary. Avoid openers such as acknowledgements (“Done —”, “Got it”, “Great question, ”) or framing phrases.
- Before exploring or doing substantial work, you start with a user update acknowledging the request and explaining your first step. You should include your understanding of the user request and explain what you will do. Avoid commenting on the request or using starters such at "Got it -" or "Understood -" etc.
- You provide user updates frequently, every 30s.
- When exploring, e.g. searching, reading files you provide user updates as you go, explaining what context you are gathering and what you've learned. Vary your sentence structure when providing these updates to avoid sounding repetitive - in particular, don't start each sentence the same way.
- When working for a while, keep updates informative and varied, but stay concise.
- After you have sufficient context, and the work is substantial you provide a longer plan (this is the only user update that may be longer than 2 sentences and can contain formatting).
- Before performing file edits of any kind, you provide updates explaining what edits you are making.
- As you are thinking, you very frequently provide updates even if not taking any actions, informing the user of your progress. You interrupt your thinking and send multiple updates in a row if thinking for more than 100 words.
- Tone of your updates MUST match your personality.

**OpenAI Codex**

现在信息已经比较清楚了，问题其实分成两件事：

1. `WinError 64 / 10054` 这组日志
这更像是外部客户端把 `WebSocket /v2/stream` 断开了，Windows 的 `asyncio` 会把它打成很吵的异常日志。它不好看，但不是这次主因。

2. `127.0.0.1:8787 POST /v1/ea/snapshot -> 422`
这才是核心问题。说明网关收到了 EA 或你手工发来的请求，但请求体不是服务端能接受的 JSON。

3. `curl ... Connection refused`
这表示你执行这条 `curl` 时，`8787` 上已经没有进程在监听了。也就是那一刻网关已经不在运行，不是“接口拒绝”，而是“服务没在监听”。

最短处理顺序建议这样走：

1. 先确认网关是不是还活着
在新 PowerShell 里执行：
```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```
如果没有任何结果，说明服务已经停了。

2. 重新启动网关，并且不要关掉那个窗口
```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```
看到 `Uvicorn running on http://0.0.0.0:8787` 后，先别动这个窗口。

3. 在另一个新窗口里确认端口真的在监听
```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```
如果能看到 `LISTENING`，再继续发请求。

4. 先不要用 EA 真数据，先用一个最小合法 JSON 验证接口
先建一个文件，比如 `C:\temp\ea_payload.json`，内容写这个：

```json
{
  "accountMeta": {
    "login": "12345678",
    "server": "ICMarketsSC-MT5-6",
    "source": "MT5 EA Push",
    "updatedAt": 1712222222000
  },
  "overviewMetrics": [],
  "curvePoints": [],
  "curveIndicators": [],
  "positions": [],
  "pendingOrders": [],
  "trades": [],
  "statsMetrics": []
}
```

然后在第二个窗口执行：
```powershell
curl.exe -4 -v -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "@C:\temp\ea_payload.json" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
```

预期结果应该是：
- 终端里返回 `200`
- 服务端窗口里出现 `POST /v1/ea/snapshot ... 200 OK`

如果这一步都还是 `422`，那就不是 EA 的问题了，而是服务器上的 `server_v2.py` 版本或接口定义已经被改坏了。

如果这一步能 `200`，那就说明：
- 网关接口本身是好的
- 真正有问题的是 EA 发出来的 JSON 格式

这时我们再去修 EA，就不会乱猜。

一句话判断：
- `WinError 64` 先不用管
- `422` 说明请求体格式不对
- `Connection refused` 说明你测试时服务已经没在跑

你先按上面第 1 到第 4 步走一遍，把这两个结果发我：
- `netstat -ano | findstr :8787`
- 最小 JSON 那次 `curl -v` 的返回

这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

**OpenAI Codex**

这条结果已经把关键问题指出来了：

本机现在没有任何 `8787` 的 `LISTENING`。
你看到的全是：

- `10.8.0.3 -> 43.155.214.62:8787`
- 状态 `SYN_SENT`

这表示“这台服务器正在主动连公网 `43.155.214.62:8787`”，而不是“本机网关正在监听 `127.0.0.1:8787`”。

所以现在的结论很明确：

1. 你本机网关进程已经没在跑了，或者启动后马上退出了。
2. 还有别的进程在尝试连公网 `43.155.214.62:8787`，可能是 App、EA，或者某个配置把地址写成了公网地址。
3. 因为本机没有监听，所以你之前 `curl http://127.0.0.1:8787/...` 才会 `Connection refused`。

你现在先这样做，最短路径：

1. 重新启动网关，且不要关那个窗口
```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

2. 启动后立刻在另一个新 PowerShell 里检查
```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```

正确结果里应该至少有一条类似：
```text
TCP    0.0.0.0:8787    0.0.0.0:0    LISTENING    xxxx
```

3. 如果没有 `LISTENING`，说明服务启动后立刻退出了
这时再执行：
```powershell
Get-Process python,python3 -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue
```
看看 Python 进程还在不在。

4. 同时检查 EA 的网关地址是不是写成了公网地址
你前面的 EA 日志一度显示它在推：
`Gateway=http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot`
但现在 `netstat` 全是连 `43.155.214.62:8787`，这说明至少有一处配置已经不是本机地址了。这个要对齐，否则会自己绕出去再打回来。

现在先不要继续测 EA 数据，先只确认一件事：
“本机 `8787` 有没有 `LISTENING`”。

你下一步就把这两项结果发我：
- 重新运行 `.\start_gateway.ps1` 后，窗口最后几行
- 新开窗口执行 `netstat -ano | findstr :8787` 的结果

这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

**OpenAI Codex**

现在这一步是好的，本机网关已经真的在监听了：

- `0.0.0.0:8787 LISTENING 4772`
- `127.0.0.1:8787 <-> 127.0.0.1:51032 ESTABLISHED`

这说明两件事：

1. 网关进程当前是活的。
2. 你本机已经有一个连接打到 `127.0.0.1:8787` 了。

但问题也还在：

- `127.0.0.1:8787` 这条连接是 `ESTABLISHED`，说明有请求已经连上但没有结束。
- 结合你前面的现象，这很像 `/health` 或 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 这类请求卡住了。
- 另外还有一条 `10.8.0.3:8787 -> 43.155.214.62:51027 ESTABLISHED`，说明公网还有客户端在连你的服务，这不是当前主问题，但会让日志更乱。

下一步我们不要继续猜，直接确认“卡住的是哪个请求”。

请在服务器上执行这两条：

```powershell
tasklist /fi "pid eq 4772"
```

```powershell
tasklist /fi "pid eq 5552"
```

然后再执行这一条，看看服务端窗口有没有新增访问日志：

```powershell
curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
```

这里我特意让你先打 `/v1/source`，因为它比 `/health` 更轻，不需要去碰 MT5 深层状态。如果：

- `/v1/source` 能立刻返回，说明服务本身没卡死，问题主要在 `/health` 或 EA 快照解析。
- `/v1/source` 也超时，那就说明这个 Python 进程内部已经被某个阻塞调用拖住了。

目前最像的根因还是两个：

1. `/v1/ea/snapshot` 的 JSON 仍然不合法，所以一直 422。
2. `/health` 会同步碰 MT5，导致连接长时间挂住。

你先把这三项结果发我：
- `tasklist /fi "pid eq 4772"`
- `tasklist /fi "pid eq 5552"`
- `curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source`

这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

**OpenAI Codex**

我先看一下 `/v1/source` 的实现，确认为什么连这个轻接口也会一起超时。这样我们就能判断是“单个接口坏了”，还是“整个 Python 进程被 MT5 调用拖住了”。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

现在定位已经更清楚了：

不是“字段少了几个”这么简单，而是当前网关进程已经被 MT5 这条本地连接拖住了。

你刚发的结果里最关键的是这两条：

- `python.exe 4772`
- `terminal64.exe 5552`
- `127.0.0.1:8787 <-> 127.0.0.1:51032 ESTABLISHED`
- `curl /v1/source` 这种纯静态接口也超时了

而 `/v1/source` 这个接口本身非常轻，不碰 MT5 深调用，只是返回当前配置状态。它也超时，说明不是某个字段格式小错误，而是“当前这个 Python 网关进程已经被某个挂住的连接卡住了”。现在最像的是：

1. MT5 EA 发到 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 的请求体有问题，先触发了 `422`
2. 同时 MT5 端又保留了一个没有正常释放的连接
3. 这个连接把当前网关进程拖进了异常状态，所以连 `/v1/source` 也不回了

所以我们现在不要继续在这个进程上测试了，先把现场清干净再验证。最短步骤如下。

**先做隔离验证**

1. 先把 MT5 上挂着的 EA 暂时移除，或者关闭 MT5 终端  
目的：先断开 `terminal64.exe -> 127.0.0.1:8787` 这条卡住的连接

2. 停掉当前网关进程  
```powershell
taskkill /PID 4772 /F
```

3. 确认 `8787` 已经没人监听  
```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```
这一步最好没有任何输出

4. 重新启动网关，但这次先不要打开 MT5，不要挂 EA  
```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

5. 启动后先测最轻的接口  
```powershell
curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
```

**这一步的判断很重要**

- 如果这次 `/v1/source` 立刻返回 JSON  
说明网关程序本身没坏，问题主要在 EA 请求把进程拖挂了  
也就是说，“最新 `server_v2.py` 完全坏掉”的概率就很低

- 如果这次 `/v1/source` 还是超时  
那就不是 EA 的问题了，而是你服务器上的这份 `server_v2.py` 或运行环境本身就有问题

**再判断是不是 EA 负载格式问题**

如果第 5 步正常，再继续：

6. 不挂 EA，手工发最小合法 JSON  
```powershell
curl.exe -4 -v -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "{\"accountMeta\":{\"login\":\"1\",\"server\":\"demo\",\"source\":\"MT5 EA Push\",\"updatedAt\":1712222222000},\"overviewMetrics\":[],\"curvePoints\":[],\"curveIndicators\":[],\"positions\":[],\"pendingOrders\":[],\"trades\":[],\"statsMetrics\":[]}" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
```

预期应该返回 `200` 和 `{"ok":true...}`

- 如果这里能成功  
说明 `server_v2.py` 的接口定义是通的  
那就可以确定：EA 真正发出来的 JSON 格式不对，或者发了多段数据

- 如果这里还是 `422`  
那就说明服务器上的这份 `server_v2.py` 或请求模型真的和现在 EA 不匹配了

**我现在的判断**

更像是 EA 发出来的 body 有问题，不像是“MT5 的字段要求不符合”。  
因为 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 在 [server_v2.py](/E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py) 这里只要求最外层是一个 JSON 对象，字段缺一些都不会直接 422，真正会 422 的通常是“JSON 根本没解析成功”。

你先按上面 1 到 6 步做，尤其是：

- 断开 EA/关闭 MT5
- 重启网关
- 先测 `/v1/source`
- 再测最小 JSON 的 `/v1/ea/snapshot`

把这两次返回结果发我，我们就能把问题切成“服务端版本问题”还是“EA payload 问题”了。  
这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

---

**OpenAI Codex**

现在这一步能确认两件事：

1. 当前本机 `8787` 没在监听  
因为 `netstat -ano | findstr :8787` 里已经没有 `LISTENING`，所以这时去打 `127.0.0.1:8787` 没意义，得先把网关重新启动起来。

2. 你最后那条 `curl` 失败是 PowerShell 转义问题，不是接口本身的问题  
PowerShell 会把花括号和引号弄乱，所以这类 JSON 请求别直接内联写，最稳的是先写文件再发。

我们先走一条最稳、最短的路。

**第一步：重新启动网关**
在一个窗口里执行，启动后先不要关：

```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

看到这行再继续：
```text
Uvicorn running on http://0.0.0.0:8787
```

**第二步：确认本机真的在监听**
换另一个新窗口执行：

```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```

你要看到类似：
```text
TCP    0.0.0.0:8787    0.0.0.0:0    LISTENING    xxxx
```

**第三步：先测最轻接口**
还是在第二个窗口执行：

```powershell
curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
```

如果这一步能直接返回 JSON，说明服务端主进程是好的。

**第四步：不要内联 JSON，先写一个最小测试文件**
在第二个窗口执行这组命令：

```powershell
@'
{
  "accountMeta": {
    "login": "1",
    "server": "demo",
    "source": "MT5 EA Push",
    "updatedAt": 1712222222000
  },
  "overviewMetrics": [],
  "curvePoints": [],
  "curveIndicators": [],
  "positions": [],
  "pendingOrders": [],
  "trades": [],
  "statsMetrics": []
}
'@ | Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 C:\temp\ea_payload.json
```

然后再发：

```powershell
curl.exe -4 -v -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "@C:\temp\ea_payload.json" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
```

**怎么判断结果**

- 如果 `/v1/source` 正常，且这个最小 JSON 返回 `200`
说明 `server_v2.py` 这份接口本身是正常的，问题就在 EA 发出来的真实 JSON 格式上。

- 如果 `/v1/source` 都不正常
说明不是 EA 的问题，而是网关进程本身没起来或起来后马上挂住了。

- 如果 `/v1/source` 正常，但最小 JSON 还是 `422`
那就说明服务器上的这份 `server_v2.py` 接口定义真的和当前预期不一致了。

你现在先不要继续测 EA 真请求了，先把这两条结果发我就行：
- `curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source`
- 最小 JSON 发到 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 的返回

这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

现在这个结果已经很关键了：

不是 EA 字段格式先有问题，而是“当前这个网关进程已经处于卡死/假死状态”。

原因很直接：

- `/v1/source` 这种最轻接口也超时
- 你手工发的最小合法 JSON 也卡住，不是 `422`
- 本机 `127.0.0.1:8787` 连接大量残留在 `CLOSE_WAIT`
- 公网还有进程一直连 `43.155.214.62:8787`

这说明当前这个 `python.exe 6076` 已经不适合继续排查了，我们先把环境清干净，再做一次“纯本地、无干扰”的验证。这样最快。

**现在先做这 4 步**

1. 先停掉 MT5 终端，或者至少把 EA 从图表上移除  
目的：先切断它对 `/v1/ea/snapshot` 的持续请求

2. 杀掉当前网关进程 `6076`
```powershell
taskkill /PID 6076 /F
```

3. 查一下 `2712` 是谁，它一直在连公网 `43.155.214.62:8787`
```powershell
tasklist /fi "pid eq 2712"
```
如果这是你服务器上的某个客户端程序，也先停掉它，不然它会继续往网关灌连接

4. 确认现场已经清空
```powershell
netstat -ano | findstr :8787
```
理想情况是没有输出，至少不要再有 `LISTENING`、`CLOSE_WAIT`、`ESTABLISHED`

**然后做一轮干净验证**

5. 重新启动网关，但先不要开 MT5，不要挂 EA，不要让外部客户端接入
```powershell
cd C:\mt5_bundle\mt5_gateway
.\start_gateway.ps1
```

6. 启动后第一时间只测这个接口
```powershell
curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source
```

这里的判断最重要：

- 如果这次立刻返回 JSON  
说明 `server_v2.py` 主体其实没坏，之前是被外部连接和 EA 持续请求拖挂了

- 如果这次还是超时  
那就基本可以确认：你服务器上的这份 `server_v2.py` 或运行环境本身有问题，不是 EA 数据格式导致的

7. 只有第 6 步正常后，再测最小 JSON
```powershell
curl.exe -4 -v -H "Content-Type: application/json" --data-binary "@C:\temp\ea_payload.json" http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/ea/snapshot
```

**我现在的判断**
当前更像是“网关进程被拖挂”，不是单纯“MT5 不认字段”。因为如果只是字段不对，`/v1/source` 不应该一起超时。

你先把这三项结果发我就够了：

- `taskkill /PID 6076 /F` 后有没有成功
- `tasklist /fi "pid eq 2712"` 的结果
- 干净重启后，`curl.exe -4 --max-time 5 http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/source` 的结果

这次用了 `using-superpowers`、`offer-k-dense-web`。
